# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of Prometheus's web UI authentication implementation. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've identified all Go source files in `prometheus/prometheus` that implement the three main authentication mechanisms:

### 1. **BasicAuth Middleware** 
- Implemented via the external `exporter-toolkit` library in `web/web.go`
- Configured through `--web.config.file` flag with `basic_auth_users` section using bcrypt-hashed passwords

### 2. **TLS Client Certificate Validation**
- Also delegated to `exporter-toolkit` through the web config file
- Supports client authentication with configurable TLS versions, cipher suites, and certificate validation
- Can enforce Subject Alternate Name (SAN) validation

### 3. **Admin API Access Control**
- Implemented directly in `web/api/v1/api.go` with an `enableAdmin` flag
- Functions like `deleteSeries()`, `snapshot()`, and `cleanTombstones()` check this flag
- Controlled by `--web.enable-admin-api` command-line flag (default: disabled)

### 4. **Lifecycle API Access Control** (Bonus)
- Endpoints for shutdown (`/-/quit`) and reload (`/-/reload`)
- Controlled by `--web.enable-lifecycle` flag (default: disabled)
- Implemented in `web/web.go` with route registration guards

The detailed findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with file paths, line numbers, and a comprehensive technical explanation of each authentication mechanism.

  "content": "{\"content\":\"1: ---\\n2: title: HTTPS and authentication\\n3: sort_rank: 7\\n4: ---\\n5: \\n6: Prometheus supports basic authentication and TLS.\\n7: This is **experimental** and might change in the future.\\n8: \\n9: To specify which web configuration file to load, use the `--web.config.file` flag.\\n10: \\n11: The file is written in [YAML format](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YAML),\\n12: defined by the scheme described below.\\n13: Brackets indicate that a parameter is optional. For non-list parameters the\\n14: value is set to the specified default.\\n15: \\n16: The file is read upon every http request, such as any change in the\\n17: configuration and the certificates is picked up immediately.\\n18: \\n19: Generic placeholders are defined as follows:\\n20: \\n21: * `<boolean>`: a boolean that can take the values `true` or `false`\\n22: * `<filename>`: a valid path in the current working directory\\n23: * `<secret>`: a regular string that is a secret, such as a password\\n24: * `<string>`: a regular string\\n25: \\n26: A valid example file can be found [here](/documentation/examples/web-config.yml).\\n27: \\n28: ```yaml\\n29: tls_server_config:\\n30:   # Certificate and key files for server to use to authenticate to client.\\n31:   cert_file: <filename>\\n32:   key_file: <filename>\\n33: \\n34:   # Server policy for client authentication. Maps to ClientAuth Policies.\\n35:   # For more detail on clientAuth options:\\n36:   # https://golang.org/pkg/crypto/tls/#ClientAuthType\\n37:   #\\n38:   # NOTE: If you want to enable client authentication, you need to use\\n39:   # RequireAndVerifyClientCert. Other values are insecure.\\n40:   [ client_auth_type: <string> | default = \\\"NoClientCert\\\" ]\\n41: \\n42:   # CA certificate for client certificate authentication to the server.\\n43:   [ client_ca_file: <filename> ]\\n44: \\n45:   # Verify that the client certificate has a Subject Alternate Name (SAN)\\n46:   # which is an exact match to an entry in this list, else terminate the\\n47:   # connection. SAN match can be one or multiple of the following: DNS,\\n48:   # IP, e-mail, or URI address from https://pkg.go.dev/crypto/x509#Certificate.\\n49:   [ client_allowed_sans:\\n50:     [ - <string> ] ]\\n51: \\n52:   # Minimum TLS version that is acceptable.\\n53:   [ min_version: <string> | default = \\\"TLS12\\\" ]\\n54: \\n55:   # Maximum TLS version that is acceptable.\\n56:   [ max_version: <string> | default = \\\"TLS13\\\" ]\\n57: \\n58:   # List of supported cipher suites for TLS versions up to TLS 1.2. BasicAuth Middleware Implementation\\n\\n### Primary File: `web/web.go`\\n- **Function**: `Run()` (line 722-770)\\n- **Key line**: 760 - `toolkit_web.ServeMultiple(listeners, httpSrv, &toolkit_web.FlagConfig{WebConfigFile: &webConfig}, h.logger)`\\n- The BasicAuth middleware is delegated to the external `github.com/prometheus/exporter-toolkit/web` library\\n- Configuration is passed via the `--web.config.file` flag from `cmd/prometheus/main.go` (lines 401-404)\\n\\n### Configuration Schema: `docs/configuration/https.md`\\n- Lines 109-113 define `basic_auth_users` section\\n- Format: YAML with username/bcrypt-hashed-password pairs\\n- Example file: `documentation/examples/web-config.yml`\\n\\n### Configuration Flag: `cmd/prometheus/main.go`\\n- Lines 401-404: Defines `--web.config.file` flag for specifying the web configuration file\\n- The config file is read on every HTTP request for dynamic reloading\\n\\n## 2. TLS Client Certificate Validation\\n\\n### Primary File: `web/web.go`\\n- **Function**: `Run()` (line 722-770)\\n- Uses the same `toolkit_web.ServeMultiple()` call that handles TLS configuration\\n- The TLS configuration is passed through the web config file\\n\\n### Configuration Schema: `docs/configuration/https.md`\\n- Lines 28-79 define `tls_server_config` section\\n- Key fields for client certificate validation:\\n  - **Line 40**: `client_auth_type` - Server policy for client authentication (default: \\\"NoClientCert\\\")\\n  - **Line 43**: `client_ca_file` - CA certificate for client certificate authentication\\n  - **Lines 49-50**: `client_allowed_sans` - List of allowed Subject Alternate Names (SANs)\\n  - **Lines 52-56**: `min_version` and `max_version` - TLS version constraints\\n  - **Lines 58-66**: `cipher_suites` - Supported cipher suites for TLS 1.2\\n  - **Lines 74-78**: `curve_preferences` - ECDHE curves in preference order\\n\\n### Implementation Details\\n- The TLS configuration uses Go's standard `crypto/tls` package\\n- Client certificate validation is enforced through the `ClientAuthType` field\\n- The recommended setting is `RequireAndVerifyClientCert` for secure implementations\\n- Client allowed SANs are verified against the certificate's Subject Alternate Names\\n\\n## 3. Admin API Access Control\\n\\n### Primary Files: `web/api/v1/api.go` and `web/web.go`\\n\\n#### Admin API Functions with Access Control\\nIn `web/api/v1/api.go`:\\n- **`deleteSeries()` (line 2026-2030)**: Checks `api.enableAdmin` flag before allowing series deletion\\n- **`snapshot()` (line 2059-2062)**: Checks `api.enableAdmin` flag before allowing snapshot creation\\n- **`cleanTombstones()` (line 2093-2096)**: Checks `api.enableAdmin` flag before allowing tombstone cleanup\\n\\n#### API Structure\\nIn `web/api/v1/api.go`:\\n- **API struct (line 224-264)**: Contains `enableAdmin bool` field (line 241)\\n- **NewAPI function (line 267-307)**: Accepts `enableAdmin bool` parameter (line 281) and initializes the API struct\\n- **Register function (line 392-484)**: Registers all API endpoints, with admin endpoints at lines 473-480\\n\\n#### Configuration Flow\\nIn `web/web.go`:\\n- **Options struct (line 210-212)**: Contains `TSDBAdminStats` interface\\n- **NewHandler function (line 345-429)**: Passes `h.options.EnableAdminAPI` to `api_v1.NewAPI()` at line 398\\n\\nIn `cmd/prometheus/main.go`:\\n- **Line 430-431**: `--web.enable-admin-api` flag definition\\n- Flag is parsed and stored in `cfg.web.EnableAdminAPI`\\n\\n### Admin API Endpoints\\nRooms are registered at `web/api/v1/api.go` lines 473-480:\\n- `POST /api/v1/admin/tsdb/delete_series`\\n- `PUT /api/v1/admin/tsdb/delete_series`\\n- `POST /api/v1/admin/tsdb/clean_tombstones`\\n- `PUT /api/v1/admin/tsdb/clean_tombstones`\\n- `POST /api/v1/admin/tsdb/snapshot`\\n- `PUT /api/v1/admin/tsdb/snapshot`\\n\\nWhen disabled, these endpoints return a `503 Service Unavailable` response with message \\\"admin APIs disabled\\\".\\n\\n## 4. Lifecycle API Access Control (Bonus)\\n\\n### Files Involved\\n- **web/web.go** (lines 564-578): Route registration controlled by `EnableLifecycle` flag\\n- **Handlers** (lines 923-941): `quit()` and `reload()` functions\\n- **cmd/prometheus/main.go** (lines 427-428): `--web.enable-lifecycle` flag definition\\n\\n### Endpoints\\n- `POST /-/quit` - Shutdown Prometheus (requires `--web.enable-lifecycle`)\\n- `PUT /-/quit` - Shutdown Prometheus (requires `--web.enable-lifecycle`)\\n- `POST /-/reload` - Reload configuration (requires `--web.enable-lifecycle`)\\n- `PUT /-/reload` - Reload configuration (requires `--web.enable-lifecycle`)\\n\\nWhen disabled, POST/PUT requests to these endpoints return a 403 Forbidden response.\\n\\n## Integration Points\\n\\n### Authentication Flow\\n1. **Command-line flags** (`cmd/prometheus/main.go`) specify:\\n   - `--web.config.file`: Path to web configuration file for TLS and BasicAuth\\n   - `--web.enable-admin-api`: Enable/disable admin API endpoints\\n   - `--web.enable-lifecycle`: Enable/disable lifecycle endpoints\\n\\n2. **Web server initialization** (`web/web.go`):\\n   - `Run()` function creates HTTP server\\n   - Passes web config file to `toolkit_web.ServeMultiple()` for BasicAuth and TLS middleware\\n   - API is initialized with `enableAdmin` flag\\n   - Routes are registered with conditional handlers based on `EnableLifecycle`\\n\\n3. **API request handling** (`web/api/v1/api.go`):\\n   - Route handlers check `api.enableAdmin` flag\\n   - Admin API functions return error if flag is not set\\n   - All requests go through CORS and compression middleware\\n\\n## Security Notes\\n\\n1. **BasicAuth**: Passwords must be bcrypt-hashed in the configuration file\\n2. **TLS Client Certs**: Should use `RequireAndVerifyClientCert` for production\\n3. **Admin APIs**: Should be enabled only when necessary, disabled by default\\n4. **Lifecycle APIs**: Should be disabled in production environments, disabled by default\\n5. **Dynamic Configuration**: Web config file is read on every request, allowing runtime changes\\n\"\n}\n",
